<p><b>Sevastopol</b> or traditionally <b>Sebastopol</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/əl/ 'le' in 'bottle'">əl</span></span>, <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/-/ affix">-</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɒ/ short 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/əl/ 'le' in 'bottle'">əl</span></span>/</a></span></span><sup id="cite_ref-MWCD_online_paywalled_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MWCD_online_paywalled-4">[4]</a></sup> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/əl/ 'le' in 'bottle'">əl</span></span>, <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/-/ affix">-</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɒ/ short 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>/</a></span></span><sup id="cite_ref-MWCD_online_paywalled_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MWCD_online_paywalled-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Севасто́поль</span>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Севасто́поль</span>&#160;; <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatar_language" title="Crimean Tatar language">Crimean Tatar</a>: <span lang="crh">Акъяр, Aqyar</span>; <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">Σεβαστούπολη, Sevastoupoli</span>) is a city located in the southwestern region of the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean Peninsula">Crimean Peninsula</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. As a result of the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation of Crimea</a> by <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, the city is administered as a <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">federal city</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a>, though <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and most of the international community continue to regard Sevastopol as a <a href="/wiki/City_with_special_status" title="City with special status">city with special status</a> within Ukraine.</p>
<p>Sevastopol has a population of <span class="nowrap">393,304 (<a href="/wiki/Crimean_Census_(2014)" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean Census (2014)">2014 Census</a>)</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-2014Census_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014Census-5">[5]</a></sup> concentrated mostly near the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Sevastopol" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay of Sevastopol">Bay of Sevastopol</a> and surrounding areas. The location and navigability of the city's harbours have made Sevastopol a strategically important <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Sevastopol" title="Port of Sevastopol">port</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naval_base" title="Naval base">naval base</a> throughout history. The city has been a home to the Russian <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Black Sea Fleet</a>, which is why it was considered as a separate city in Crimea of significant military importance and was therefore once a <a href="/wiki/Closed_city" title="Closed city">closed city</a>.</p>
<p>Although relatively small at 864 square kilometres (334&#160;sq&#160;mi), Sevastopol's unique naval and maritime features provide the basis for a robust economy. The city enjoys mild winters and moderate warm summers; characteristics that help make it a popular <a href="/wiki/Seaside_resort" title="Seaside resort">seaside resort</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourist</a> destination, mainly for visitors <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">from the former Soviet republics</a>. The city is also an important centre for <a href="/wiki/Marine_biology" title="Marine biology">marine biology</a>; in particular, <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphins</a> have been studied and trained in the city since the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name of Sevastopolis was originally chosen in the same <a href="/wiki/Etymology" title="Etymology">etymological</a> trend as other cities in the Crimean peninsula that was intended to reflect its ancient Greek origins. It is a compound of the Greek adjective, <span lang="grc">σεβαστός</span> (<i><a href="/wiki/Sebastos" title="Sebastos">sebastos</a></i>, 'venerable') and the noun <span lang="grc">πόλις</span> (<i>pólis</i>) ('city'). <span lang="grc">Σεβαστός</span> is the traditional Greek equivalent of the Roman honorific <i><a href="/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)" title="Augustus (honorific)">Augustus</a></i>, originally given to the first emperor of the Roman Empire, <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> and later awarded as a title to his successors.</p>
<p>Despite its Greek origin, the name itself is not from Ancient Greek times. The city was probably named after the Empress ("<i><a href="/wiki/Augusta_(honorific)" class="mw-redirect" title="Augusta (honorific)">Augusta</a></i>") <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine II</a> of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> who founded Sevastopol in 1783. She visited the city in 1787 accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph II</a>, the Emperor of Austria, and other foreign dignitaries.</p>
<p>In the west of the city, there are well-preserved ruins of the ancient Greek port city of <a href="/wiki/Chersonesos_Taurica" class="mw-redirect" title="Chersonesos Taurica">Chersonesos</a>, founded in the 5th<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> (or 4th) century BC by settlers from <a href="/wiki/Heraclea_Pontica" title="Heraclea Pontica">Heraclea Pontica</a>. This name means "peninsula", reflecting its immediate location, and is not related to the ancient Greek name for the Crimean Peninsula as a whole: <i>Chersonēsos <a href="/wiki/Taurica" class="mw-redirect" title="Taurica">Taurikē</a></i> ("the <a href="/wiki/Tauri" title="Tauri">Taurian</a> Peninsula").</p>
<p>The name of the city is spelled as:</p>
<ul>
<li>In English, the current prevalent spelling of the name is <i>Sevastopol</i>; the previously common spelling <i>Sebastopol</i> is still used by some publications such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>. In English the current spelling has the pronunciation <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/əl/ 'le' in 'bottle'">əl</span></span>/</a></span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-OED-US_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OED-US-6">[6]</a></sup> whilst the former spelling has the pronunciation <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɪ/ or /ə/ 'e' in 'roses'">ᵻ</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/əl/ 'le' in 'bottle'">əl</span></span>, <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/-/ affix">-</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɒ/ short 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>/</a></span></span><sup id="cite_ref-OED-b_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OED-b-7">[7]</a></sup> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>, <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/-/ affix">-</span><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɔː/ 'au' in 'fraud'">ɔː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>/</a></span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-OED-US-b_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OED-US-b-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Севастополь</span>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Севастополь</span>, pronounced <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Ukrainian" title="Help:IPA for Ukrainian">[sevɑsˈtɔpɔlʲ]</a></span> in Ukrainian and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Russian" title="Help:IPA for Russian">[sʲɪvɐsˈtopəlʲ]</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-OED_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OED-9">[9]</a></sup> in Russian.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatar_language" title="Crimean Tatar language">Crimean Tatar</a>: <span lang="crh">Aqyar</span>, pronounced <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[aqˈjar]</a></span>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Crimea" title="History of Crimea">History of Crimea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sevastopol_04-14_img36_Chersonesus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Sevastopol_04-14_img36_Chersonesus.jpg/220px-Sevastopol_04-14_img36_Chersonesus.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Sevastopol_04-14_img36_Chersonesus.jpg/330px-Sevastopol_04-14_img36_Chersonesus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Sevastopol_04-14_img36_Chersonesus.jpg/440px-Sevastopol_04-14_img36_Chersonesus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sevastopol_04-14_img36_Chersonesus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The ruins of the ancient Greek theater in <a href="/wiki/Chersonesos_Taurica" class="mw-redirect" title="Chersonesos Taurica">Chersonesos Taurica</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 6th century BC a Greek colony was established in the area of the modern day city. The Greek city of <a href="/wiki/Chersonesus_(Crimea)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chersonesus (Crimea)">Chersonesus</a> existed for almost two thousand years, first as an independent democracy and later as part of the <a href="/wiki/Bosporan_Kingdom" title="Bosporan Kingdom">Bosporan Kingdom</a>. In the 13th and 14th centuries it was sacked by the Mongol Horde several times and was finally totally abandoned. The modern day city of Sevastopol has no connection to the ancient and medieval Greek city, but the ruins are a popular tourist attraction located on the outskirts of the city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Under_the_Russian_Empire">Under the Russian Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Under the Russian Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2012-09-09_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BC%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BB%D1%8F%D0%BC_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B5_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Monument to the ships scuttled during the siege of Sevastopol during the Crimean War by <a href="/wiki/Amandus_Adamson" title="Amandus Adamson">Amandus Adamson</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sevastopol was founded in June 1783 as a base for a naval squadron under the name Akhtiar<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> (<i>White Cliff</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> by Rear Admiral <a href="/wiki/Thomas_MacKenzie_(Russian_admiral)" title="Thomas MacKenzie (Russian admiral)">Thomas MacKenzie</a> (Foma Fomich Makenzi), a native <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scot</a> in Russian service; soon after <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> annexed the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a>. Five years earlier, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Suvorov" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleksandr Suvorov">Alexander Suvorov</a> ordered that earthworks be erected along the harbour and Russian troops be placed there. In February 1784, <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a> ordered <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Potyomkin" class="mw-redirect" title="Grigory Potyomkin">Grigory Potemkin</a> to build a fortress there and call it Sevastopol. The realisation of the initial building plans fell to Captain <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Ushakov" title="Fyodor Ushakov">Fyodor Ushakov</a> who in 1788 was named commander of the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Sevastopol" title="Port of Sevastopol">port</a> and of the Black Sea squadron.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> It became an important <a href="/wiki/Naval_base" title="Naval base">naval base</a> and later a commercial <a href="/wiki/Seaport" class="mw-redirect" title="Seaport">seaport</a>. In 1797, under an edict issued by Emperor <a href="/wiki/Paul_I_of_Russia" title="Paul I of Russia">Paul I</a>, the military stronghold was again renamed to Akhtiar. Finally, on April 29 (May 10), 1826, the Senate returned the city's name to Sevastopol.</p>
<p>One of the most notable events involving the city is the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sevastopol_(1854%E2%80%931855)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Sevastopol (1854–1855)">Siege of Sevastopol (1854–55)</a> carried out by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Turkey">Turkish</a> troops during the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>, which lasted for 11 months. Despite its efforts, the Russian army had to leave its stronghold and evacuate over a pontoon bridge to the north shore of the inlet. The Russians chose to sink their entire fleet to prevent it from falling into the hands of the enemy and at the same time to block the entrance of the Western ships into the inlet. When the enemy troops entered Sevastopol, they were faced with the ruins of a formerly glorious city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Panorama" title="Panorama">panorama</a> of the siege originally was created by <a href="/wiki/Franz_Roubaud" title="Franz Roubaud">Franz Roubaud</a>. After its destruction in 1942 during WWII, it was restored and is currently housed in a specially constructed circular building in the city. It portrays the situation at the height of the siege, on 18 June 1855.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Under_the_Soviet_Union">Under the Soviet Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Under the Soviet Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Sevastopol withstood intensive bombardment by the Germans in 1941–42, supported by their Italian and Romanian allies during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sevastopol" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Sevastopol">Battle of Sevastopol</a>. German forces were forced to use <a href="/wiki/Railway_artillery" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway artillery">railway artillery</a> — including history's largest-ever calibre railway artillery piece in battle, the 80-cm calibre <i><a href="/wiki/Schwerer_Gustav" title="Schwerer Gustav">Schwerer Gustav</a></i> — and <a href="/wiki/Karl-Ger%C3%A4t" title="Karl-Gerät">specialised mobile heavy mortars</a> to destroy Sevastopol's extremely heavy fortifications, such as the <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Gorky" title="Maxim Gorky">Maxim Gorky</a> naval battery. After fierce fighting, which lasted for 250 days, the supposedly untakable<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> fortress city finally fell to Axis forces in July 1942. It was intended to be renamed to "<i>Theoderichshafen</i>" (in reference to <a href="/wiki/Theoderic_the_Great" title="Theoderic the Great">Theoderic the Great</a> and the fact that the Crimea had been home to Germanic <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a> until the 18th or 19th century) in the event of a German victory against the Soviet Union, and like the rest of the Crimea was designated for future colonisation by the Third Reich. It was liberated by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> on May 9, 1944 and was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Hero_City" title="Hero City">Hero City</a> title a year later.</p>
<p>In 1957, the town of <a href="/wiki/Balaklava" title="Balaklava">Balaklava</a> was incorporated into Sevastopol.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sevastopol_as_part_of_Ukrainian_SSR">Sevastopol as part of Ukrainian SSR</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sevastopol as part of Ukrainian SSR">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> era, Sevastopol became a so-called "<a href="/wiki/Closed_city" title="Closed city">closed city</a>". This meant that any non-residents had to apply to the authorities for a temporary permit to visit the city.</p>
<p>On October 29, 1948 the Presidium of Supreme Council of the Russian SFSR issued an <i>ukase</i> (order) which confirmed the special status of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-myths_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myths-13">[13]</a></sup> Soviet academic publications since 1954, including the <a href="/wiki/Great_Soviet_Encyclopedia" title="Great Soviet Encyclopedia">Great Soviet Encyclopedia</a>, indicated that Sevastopol, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Oblast" title="Crimean Oblast">Crimean Oblast</a> was part of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Great_Soviet_Encyclopedia" title="Great Soviet Encyclopedia">Great Soviet Encyclopedia</a></i> 1976, Vol.23. pp 104).<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the 1955 Ukrainian parliamentary elections on February 27, Sevastopol was split into two electoral districts, Stalinsky and Korabelny (initially requested three Stalinsky, Korabelny, and Nakhimovsky).<sup id="cite_ref-myths_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myths-13">[13]</a></sup> Eventually Sevastopol received two <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Deputy_of_Ukraine" title="People's Deputy of Ukraine">people's deputies</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a> elected to the <a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada" title="Verkhovna Rada">Verkhovna Rada</a> A.Korovchenko and M.Kulakov.<sup id="cite_ref-myths_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myths-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_Soviet_dissolution">After the Soviet dissolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: After the Soviet dissolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg/220px-%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg/330px-%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg/440px-%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2795" data-file-height="1888" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%A7%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D1%84%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Black Sea Fleet Museum</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On July 10, 1993, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian parliament">Russian parliament</a> passed a resolution declaring Sevastopol to be "a federal Russian city".<sup id="cite_ref-doyle_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doyle-16">[16]</a></sup> At the time, many supporters of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">president</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a>, had ceased taking part in the Parliament's work.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> On July 20, 1993 the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> denounced the decision of the Russia parliament. According to <a href="/wiki/Anatoliy_Zlenko" title="Anatoliy Zlenko">Anatoliy Zlenko</a>, it was for the first time that the council had to review actions and come up with qualification of them for a legislative body.<sup id="cite_ref-myths_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-myths-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 14, 1993, the Presidium of the Crimean Parliament called for the creation of the presidential post of the Crimean Republic. A week later, the Russian deputy, Valentin Agafonov, stated that Russia was ready to supervise the referendum on Crimean independence and include the republic as a separate entity in the CIS. On July 28, 1993, one of the leaders of the Russian Society of Crimea, Viktor Prusakov, stated that his organisation was ready for an armed mutiny and establishment of the Russian administration in Sevastopol. In September, Eduard Baltin accused Ukraine of converting some of his fleet and conducting an armed assault on his personnel, and threatened to take countermeasures of placing the fleet on alert.</p>
<p>In May 1997, Russia and Ukraine signed the Peace and Friendship Treaty, ruling out Moscow's territorial claims to Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> A separate agreement established the terms of a long-term lease of land, facilities, and resources in Sevastopol and the Crimea by Russia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_in_Ukraine_28-29_July_2001-17.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Vladimir_Putin_in_Ukraine_28-29_July_2001-17.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_in_Ukraine_28-29_July_2001-17.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Vladimir_Putin_in_Ukraine_28-29_July_2001-17.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_in_Ukraine_28-29_July_2001-17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Vladimir_Putin_in_Ukraine_28-29_July_2001-17.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_in_Ukraine_28-29_July_2001-17.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_in_Ukraine_28-29_July_2001-17.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> with Ukrainian President <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Kuchma" title="Leonid Kuchma">Leonid Kuchma</a> on board the Black Sea Fleet's flagship, July 2001</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The ex-Soviet <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Black Sea Fleet</a> and its facilities were divided between Russia's Black Sea Fleet and the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Navy" title="Ukrainian Navy">Ukrainian Naval Forces</a>. The two navies co-used some of the city's harbours and piers, while others were demilitarised or used by either country. Sevastopol remained the location of the Russian Black Sea Fleet headquarters with the Ukrainian Naval Forces Headquarters also based in the city. A judicial row periodically continues over the naval <a href="/wiki/Hydrography" title="Hydrography">hydrographic</a> infrastructure both in Sevastopol and on the Crimean coast (especially <a href="/wiki/Lighthouses" class="mw-redirect" title="Lighthouses">lighthouses</a> historically maintained by the Soviet or Russian Navy and also used for civil navigation support).</p>
<p>As in the rest of the Crimea, Russian remained the predominant language of the city, although following the independence of Ukraine there was some attempts at <a href="/wiki/Ukrainisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainisation">Ukrainisation</a> with very little success. The Russian society in general and even some outspoken government representatives never accepted the loss of Sevastopol and tended to regard it as temporarily separated from the homeland.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2009, the chairman of the Sevastopol city council, Valeriy Saratov (<a href="/wiki/Party_of_Regions" title="Party of Regions">Party of Regions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> stated that Ukraine should increase the amount of compensation it is paying to the city of Sevastopol for hosting the foreign <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Black Sea Fleet</a>, instead of requesting such obligations from the Russian government and the Russian Ministry of Defense in particular.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 27, 2010, Russia and Ukraine ratified the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Ukrainian_Naval_Base_for_Gas_treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Ukrainian Naval Base for Gas treaty">Russian Ukrainian Naval Base for Gas treaty</a>, extending the Russian Navy's lease of Crimean facilities for 25 years after 2017 (through 2042) with an option to prolong the lease in 5-year extensions. The ratification process in the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian parliament">Ukrainian parliament</a> encountered stiff opposition and erupted into a brawl in the parliament chamber. Eventually, the treaty was ratified by a 52% majority vote—236 of 450. The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Duma" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Duma">Russian Duma</a> ratified the treaty by a 98% majority without incident.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_Crimean_crisis">2014 Crimean crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2014 Crimean crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov,_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg/220px-Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg/330px-Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg/440px-Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="4091" data-file-height="2722" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov,_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Konstantinov_(politician)" title="Vladimir Konstantinov (politician)">Vladimir Konstantinov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Aksyonov" title="Sergey Aksyonov">Sergey Aksyonov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aleksei_Chalyi" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleksei Chalyi">Aleksei Chalyi</a> signing the Treaty, March 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2014_Crimean_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Crimean crisis">2014 Crimean crisis</a></div>
<p>On March 6, 2014, in response to the <a href="/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution" title="2014 Ukrainian revolution">2014 Ukrainian revolution</a>, the city council of Sevastopol unilaterally declared that it wished to join the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Federal_subject" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal subject">federal subject</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The city council on 11 March released a <a href="/wiki/Joint_resolution" title="Joint resolution">joint resolution</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Council of Crimea">Supreme Council of Crimea</a> to unite as an independent republic between the potential passing of the referendum and union with Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Ukrainian authorities and the international community strongly criticized the referendum decision.<sup id="cite_ref-turchynov_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turchynov-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 16, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_referendum,_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean referendum, 2014">a controversial referendum</a> on leaving Ukraine took place in the city, along with the rest of Crimea. During the voting the <a href="/wiki/Building_of_the_Supreme_Council_of_Crimea" title="Building of the Supreme Council of Crimea">Building of the Supreme Council of Crimea</a> was controlled by the Russian military.<sup id="cite_ref-turchynov_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turchynov-25">[25]</a></sup> The official reports by the organizers of the referendum were that a majority of 95.6%<sup id="cite_ref-sevsovet_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sevsovet-26">[26]</a></sup> voted to become a part of the Russian Federation,though these results <a href="/wiki/Crimean_status_referendum,_2014#Alternative_estimates_of_results" title="Crimean status referendum, 2014">are contested</a>. This referendum resulted in the establishment of the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea_(country)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Crimea (country)">Republic of Crimea</a>, which consisted of both Sevastopol and Crimea.</p>
<p>On March 18, 2014, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Crimea_to_the_Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Accession of Crimea to the Russian Federation">the treaty on the adoption of the Republic of Crimea and Sevastopol to Russia</a> was signed between Russia and the Republic of Crimea, with the following content:<sup id="cite_ref-Treaty_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Treaty-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The territory of the former <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Autonomous Republic of Crimea">Autonomous Republic of Crimea</a> is incorporated as the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">Federal subject of Russian Federation</a>).</li>
<li>The former <a href="/wiki/City_with_special_status_(Ukraine)" class="mw-redirect" title="City with special status (Ukraine)">Special Status City of Sevastopol</a> is incorporated as a <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">Federal City of Russia</a>.</li>
<li>Both territories are incorporated as part of the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Federal_District" title="Crimean Federal District">Crimean Federal District</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>This new status is not internationally recognised. Crimea and Sevastopol is still considered by Ukraine, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, most nations and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sevastopol,_Ukraine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Sevastopol%2C_Ukraine.jpg/220px-Sevastopol%2C_Ukraine.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Sevastopol%2C_Ukraine.jpg/330px-Sevastopol%2C_Ukraine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Sevastopol%2C_Ukraine.jpg/440px-Sevastopol%2C_Ukraine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="1440" /></a>

Satellite image of the Sevastopol area.</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Fiolent_Sevastopol_2009_G1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Fiolent_Sevastopol_2009_G1.jpg/300px-Fiolent_Sevastopol_2009_G1.jpg" width="300" height="225" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Fiolent_Sevastopol_2009_G1.jpg/450px-Fiolent_Sevastopol_2009_G1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Fiolent_Sevastopol_2009_G1.jpg/600px-Fiolent_Sevastopol_2009_G1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2950" data-file-height="2215" /></a></div>

</div>

</div>
<p>The city of Sevastopol is located at the southwestern tip of the Crimean peninsula in a headland known as <a href="/wiki/Heracles_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Heracles peninsula">Heracles peninsula</a> on a coast of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. The city is designated a special city-region of Ukraine which beside the city itself includes several of its outlying settlements. The city itself is concentrated mostly at the western portion of the region and around the long <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Sevastopol" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay of Sevastopol">Bay of Sevastopol</a>. This bay is a <a href="/wiki/Ria" title="Ria">ria</a>, a river canyon drowned by <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">Holocene</a> sea-level rise, and the outlet of <a href="/wiki/Chorna_River_(Crimea)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chorna River (Crimea)">Chorna River</a>. Away in a remote location southeast of Sevastopol is located the former city of <a href="/wiki/Balaklava" title="Balaklava">Balaklava</a> (since 1957 incorporated within Sevastopol), the bay of which in Soviet times served as a main port for the Soviet diesel-powered submarines.</p>
<p>The coastline of the region is mostly rocky, in a series of smaller bays, a great number of which are located within the Bay of Sevastopol. The biggest of them are the Southern Bay (within Bay of Sevastopol), the Archer Bay, a gulf complex that consist of the Deergrass Bay, the Bay of Cossack, the Salty Bay, and many others. There are over thirty bays in the immediate region.</p>
<p>Through the region flow three rivers: the Belbek, Chorna, and Kacha. All three mountain chains of <a href="/wiki/Crimean_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean mountains">Crimean mountains</a> are represented in Sevastopol, the southern chain by the Balaklava Highlands, the inner chain by the Mekenziev Mountains, and the outer chain by the Kara-Tau Upland (Black Mountain).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sevastopol has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <i>Cfa</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-koppen_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-koppen-29">[29]</a></sup> thanks to summer mean straddling 22&#160;°C (72&#160;°F) that is bordering on a four-season <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>, with cool winters and warm to hot summers.</p>
<p>The average yearly temperature is 15–16&#160;°C (59–61&#160;°F) during the day and around 9&#160;°C (48&#160;°F) at night. In the coldest months, January and February, the average temperature is 5–6&#160;°C (41–43&#160;°F) during the day and around 1&#160;°C (34&#160;°F) at night. In the warmest months, July and August, the average temperature is around 26&#160;°C (79&#160;°F) during the day and around 19&#160;°C (66&#160;°F) at night. Generally, summer/holiday season lasts 5 months, from around mid-May and into September, with the temperature often reaching 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F) or more in the first half of October.</p>
<p>The average annual temperature of the sea is 14.2&#160;°C (58&#160;°F), ranging from 7&#160;°C (45&#160;°F) in February to 24&#160;°C (75&#160;°F) in August. From June to September, the average sea temperature is greater than 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F). In the second half of May and first half of October; the average sea temperature is about 17&#160;°C (63&#160;°F). The average rainfall is about 400 millimetres (16&#160;in) per year. There are about 2,345 hours of sunshine duration per year.<sup id="cite_ref-meteoweb_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meteoweb-30">[30]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:608px;max-width:608px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">

<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Navy" title="Ukrainian Navy">Ukrainian Navy</a> artillery boat U170 in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Sevastopol" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay of Sevastopol">Bay of Sevastopol</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1954, both Sevastopol and the remainder of the Crimean peninsula were administratively transferred by <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> from being territories within the Russian SFSR to being territories administered by the Ukrainian SSR. Administratively, Sevastopol was a municipality excluded from the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Autonomous Republic of Crimea">Autonomous Republic of Crimea</a>. The territory of the municipality was 863.5&#160;km² and it was further subdivided into four raions (districts). Besides the City of Sevastopol proper, it also included two towns—Balaklava (having had no status until 1957), Inkerman, urban-type settlement Kacha, and 29 villages. Until recently, Sevastopol had no elected mayor, instead a "Chairman of the Sevastopol City State Administration", would be appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">President of Ukraine</a>, and functioned as a mayor.<sup id="cite_ref-YavlinskyUkr_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YavlinskyUkr-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of December 2014 the political status of Sevastopol remains uncertain, with most of the international community recognizing the city as part of Ukraine, while it is de facto controlled by Russia.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_(2493-07).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-07%29.jpg/220px-Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-07%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-07%29.jpg/330px-Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-07%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-07%29.jpg/440px-Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_%282493-07%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="434" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Celebrating_Victory_Day_and_the_70th_anniversary_of_Sevastopol%E2%80%99s_liberation_(2493-07).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Victory Day in Sevastopol, 9 May 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On March 18, 2014 the Kremlin announced that Sevastopol will become the third <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">federal city</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a>. The two others are Moscow and St. Petersburg.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_State_Administration">City State Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: City State Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The executive power of Sevastopol is exercised by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol_City_State_Administration&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sevastopol City State Administration (page does not exist)">Sevastopol City State Administration</a> led by a chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Since April 2014 the executive power is held by the Government of Sevastopol, led by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Sevastopol_(Russia)" title="Governor of Sevastopol (Russia)">City Governor</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_Council">City Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: City Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol_City_Council" title="Sevastopol City Council">Sevastopol City Council</a> is the legislature of Sevastopol. Under Ukrainian law, the mayor of Sevastopol is appointed by the central government in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>. However, during the <a href="/wiki/2014_Crimean_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Crimean crisis">2014 Crimean crisis</a>, the pro-Russian City Council threw its support behind Russian citizen <a href="/wiki/Alexei_Chaly" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexei Chaly">Alexei Chaly</a> as the "people's mayor" and said it would not recognise orders from Kiev.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Crimea_to_the_Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Accession of Crimea to the Russian Federation">Accession of Crimea to the Russian Federation</a>, the mayor is appointed by the legislature branch on nomination of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">Russian President</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> and officially the mayor is called the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Sevastopol_(Russia)" title="Governor of Sevastopol (Russia)">Governor of Sevastopol City</a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_and_municipal_divisions">Administrative and municipal divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Administrative and municipal divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_and_municipal_divisions_of_Sevastopol" title="Administrative and municipal divisions of Sevastopol">Administrative and municipal divisions of Sevastopol</a></div>
<p>Being a disputed territory, Sevastopol has two sets of laws governing how its administrative and municipal divisions are set up. Under both Ukrainian and Russian laws, the city is administratively divided into four districts.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sevastopol-boroughs.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Sevastopol-boroughs.svg/220px-Sevastopol-boroughs.svg.png" width="220" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Sevastopol-boroughs.svg/330px-Sevastopol-boroughs.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Sevastopol-boroughs.svg/440px-Sevastopol-boroughs.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="375" data-file-height="457" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sevastopol-boroughs.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Districts of Sevastopol:
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #F09ABD; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Gagarin_Raion" class="mw-redirect" title="Gagarin Raion">Gagarin Raion</a> (Gagarinsky District)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #E14A35; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Lenin_Raion,_Sevastopol" title="Lenin Raion, Sevastopol">Lenin Raion</a> (Leninsky District)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #45B7ED; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Nakhimov_Raion" title="Nakhimov Raion">Nakhimov Raion</a> (Nakhimovsky District)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8DCCA1; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Balaklava_Raion" title="Balaklava Raion">Balaklava Raion</a> (Balaklavsky District)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Under the Ukrainian laws, the districts have both administrative and municipal status, while under the Russian laws the districts are purely administrative and have no further divisions. Within the Russian <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Russia#Municipal_divisions" title="Subdivisions of Russia">municipal framework</a>, however, the territory of the federal city of Sevastopol is divided into nine <a href="/wiki/Okrug#Russian_Federation" title="Okrug">municipal okrugs</a> and the Town of Inkerman. While individual municipal divisions are contained within the borders of the administrative districts, they are not otherwise related to the administrative districts.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-notice" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w.svg" class="image"><img alt="Wiki letter w.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/44px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png" width="44" height="44" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/66px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/88px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="44" /></a></div>

<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>is missing information about Sevastopol's economic output by <a href="/wiki/Economic_sector" title="Economic sector">economic sector</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please expand the section to include this information. </tr>
</table>
<p>Apart from navy-related civil facilities, Sevastopol hosts some other notable industries. An example is Stroitel, one of the leading <a href="/wiki/Plastic" title="Plastic">plastic</a> manufacturers in Russia.</p>
<p>The city received millions of US Dollars in compensation for hosting the Russian Black Sea Fleet from the Russian and the Ukrainian government.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Trolleybus_Sevastopol_2012_G2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Trolleybus_Sevastopol_2012_G2.jpg/220px-Trolleybus_Sevastopol_2012_G2.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Trolleybus_Sevastopol_2012_G2.jpg/330px-Trolleybus_Sevastopol_2012_G2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Trolleybus_Sevastopol_2012_G2.jpg/440px-Trolleybus_Sevastopol_2012_G2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4800" data-file-height="2850" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Trolleybus_Sevastopol_2012_G2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">Trolleybuses</a> <a href="/wiki/ZiU-9" title="ZiU-9">ZiU-9</a> in Sevastopol</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are 7 types of transport in Sevastopol:</p>
<ul>
<li>Bus – 101 lines</li>
<li>Trolleybus – 14 lines</li>
<li>Minibus – 52 lines</li>
<li>Cutter – 6 lines</li>
<li>Ferry – 1 lines</li>
<li>Express-bus – 15 lines</li>
<li>HEV-train{local, suburban route} – 1 route</li>
<li>Airport - 1</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sevastopol_Shipyard" title="Sevastopol Shipyard">Sevastopol Shipyard</a> comprises three facilities that together repair, modernize, and re-equip Russian Naval ships and submarines.<sup id="cite_ref-fas_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fas-38">[38]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol_International_Airport" title="Sevastopol International Airport">Sevastopol International Airport</a> is used as a military aerodrome at the moment and being reconstructed to be used by international airlines.</p>
<p>Sevastopol maintains a large port facility in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Sevastopol" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay of Sevastopol">Bay of Sevastopol</a> and in smaller bays around the <a href="/wiki/Heracles_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Heracles peninsula">Heracles peninsula</a>. The port handles traffic from passengers (local transportation and cruise), cargo, and commercial fishing. The port infrastructure is fully integrated with the city of Sevastopol and naval bases of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Black Sea Fleet</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1008px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sevastopol_panorama.JPG" class="image" title="Panorama of the Sevastopol port entrance (left) with its monument to Russian ships which were sunk in the Crimean war to blockade the harbor (far right side)."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Sevastopol_panorama.JPG/1000px-Sevastopol_panorama.JPG" width="1000" height="258" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Sevastopol_panorama.JPG/1500px-Sevastopol_panorama.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Sevastopol_panorama.JPG/2000px-Sevastopol_panorama.JPG 2x" data-file-width="7108" data-file-height="1832" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sevastopol_panorama.JPG" title="File:Sevastopol panorama.JPG"></a></div>
Panorama of the Sevastopol port entrance (left) with its monument to <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russian_Navy" title="Imperial Russian Navy">Russian ships</a> which were sunk in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean war">Crimean war</a> to blockade the <a href="/wiki/Harbor" title="Harbor">harbor</a> (far right side).</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Sevastopol was entirely rebuilt. Many top architects and civil engineers from Moscow, Leningrad, Kiev and other cities and thousands of workers from all parts of the USSR took part in the rebuilding process which was mostly finished by the mid-1950s. The downtown core situated on a peninsula between two narrow inlets, South Bay and Artillery Bay, features mostly Mediterranean-style, three-story residential buildings with columned balconies and Venetian-style arches, with retail and commercial spaces occupying the ground level. Some carefully restored landmarks date back to the early 20th century (e.g., the Art Nouveau Main Post Office on Bolshaya Morskaya St and the Art Museum on Nakhimovsky Prospect). It has been a long-time tradition for the residents of surrounding suburbs to spend summer evenings by coming to the downtown area for a leisurely stroll with their families along the avenues and boulevards encircling the Central Hill, under the famous Sevastopol chestnut trees, and usually ending up on the waterfront with its famous Marine Boulevard.</p>
<p>Due to its military history, most streets in the city are named after Russian and Soviet military heroes. There are hundreds of monuments and plaques in various parts of Sevastopol commemorating its military past.</p>
<p>Attractions include:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chersonesos_Taurica" class="mw-redirect" title="Chersonesos Taurica">Chersonessos</a> National Archeological Reserve</li>
<li>Sevastopol Art Museum named after the N.P.Kroshitskiy</li>
<li>Sevastopol Museum of Local History</li>
<li>Aquarium-Museum of the Institute of Biology of the Southern Seas of the National Academy of Sciences of Ukraine</li>
<li>Dolphinarium of Sevastopol</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sevastopol_Zoo" title="Sevastopol Zoo">Sevastopol Zoo</a></li>
<li>The Monument to the scuttled ships on the Marine Boulevard</li>
<li>The Panorama Museum (The Heroic Defence of Sevastopol during the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Malakhov_Kurgan" class="mw-redirect" title="Malakhov Kurgan">Malakhov Kurgan</a> (Barrow) with its White Tower</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Admirals%27_Burial_Vault" class="mw-redirect" title="Admirals' Burial Vault">Admirals' Burial Vault</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Black Sea Fleet</a> Museum</li>
<li>The Storming of <a href="/wiki/Sapun-gora" class="mw-redirect" title="Sapun-gora">Sapun-gora</a> of May 7, 1944, the Diorama Museum (<a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>)</li>
<li>Naval museum complex "<a href="/wiki/Naval_museum_complex_Balaklava" title="Naval museum complex Balaklava">Balaklava</a>", decommissioned underground submarine base, now opened to the public</li>
<li>Cheremetieff brothers museum "Crimean war 1853-1856"</li>
<li>Museum of the underground forces of 1942—1944</li>
<li>Museum Historical Memorial Complex <a href="/wiki/35th_coastal_battery" title="35th coastal battery">"35th Coastal Battery"</a></li>
<li>The Naval Museum "Michael's battery"</li>
<li>Fraternal (Communal) War Cemetery (Sevastopol)</li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-notice" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w.svg" class="image"><img alt="Wiki letter w.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/44px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png" width="44" height="44" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/66px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/88px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="44" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>is missing information about the different religions practiced in Sevastopol; its education system (schools, colleges, and universities); and its healthcare system (clinics and hospitals)</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please expand the section to include this information. Further details may exist on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Sevastopol" title="Talk:Sevastopol">talk page</a>.</span> <small><i>(March 2014)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The population of Sevastopol proper is 418,987 (01.01.16),<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> making it the 46th largest city in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and the largest in <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a>. City agglomeration has population ~600,000 (2015). According to the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Census_(2001)" title="Ukrainian Census (2001)">Ukrainian National Census, 2001</a>, the ethnic groups of Sevastopol include <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> (71.6%), <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> (22.4%), <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a> (1.6%), <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a> (0.7%), <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a> (0.5%), <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a> (0.3%), <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jews</a> (0.3%), <a href="/wiki/Moldovans" title="Moldovans">Moldovans</a> (0.2%), and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani people">Azerbaijanis</a> (0.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-census_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-40">[40]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sevastopol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-notice" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w.svg" class="image"><img alt="Wiki letter w.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/44px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png" width="44" height="44" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/66px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/88px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="44" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>is missing information about architecture, arts, cuisine, literature, media, and music in Sevastopol</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please expand the section to include this information. Further details may exist on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Sevastopol" title="Talk:Sevastopol">talk page</a>.</span> <small><i>(March 2014)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>There are many historical buildings in the central and eastern parts of the city and Balaklava, some of which are architectural monuments. The Western districts have modern architecture. More recently, numerous skyscrapers have been built. Balaklava Bayfront Plaza (On Hold), currently under construction, will be one of the tallest buildings in Ukraine, at 173&#160;m (568&#160;ft) with 43 floors.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/2014_Russian_annexation_of_Crimea" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Russian annexation of Crimea">2014 Russian annexation of Crimea</a> the city's monument to <a href="/wiki/Petro_Konashevych-Sahaidachny" title="Petro Konashevych-Sahaidachny">Petro Konashevych-Sahaidachny</a> was removed and handed over to <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv" title="Kharkiv">Kharkiv</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/2121_Sevastopol" title="2121 Sevastopol">2121 Sevastopol</a> – <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">asteroid</a> discovered in 1971 by <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> astronomer <a href="/wiki/Tamara_Mikhailovna_Smirnova" class="mw-redirect" title="Tamara Mikhailovna Smirnova">Tamara Mikhailovna Smirnova</a> and named after the city.<sup id="cite_ref-minorplanet_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minorplanet-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
